Topic - *Presentation*

Among the following given topics,   choose any one for presentation.

1. Tablet
2. Lotion 
3. Gel
4. Ointment
5. Cream
6. Antibiotics 
7. Syrup
8. Nassal Spray.

 *How to present it* 
 *1st slide* will be introduction of students
 *2nd slide* introduction of chosen topic
 *3rd slide* use of  chosen topic
 *4th slide* Advantages , disadvantages and ingredients of chosen topics.
 *5th slide* Add some questions for Audience & Express Thanks

 *Use PPT or print of PPT for presentation*

 *Thanks and Regards* 
Kuldeep Dharpawar
English Lecturer
4/24/25, 5:03 PM - Sarvesh: He karyla kiti time lagel tula?
4/24/25, 5:13 PM - Sarvesh: Slide 3: Uses of TabletsMedical Uses:Treat diseases (e.g., paracetamol for pain, metformin for diabetes).Preventive (e.g., vitamins, supplements).Controlled-release for long-term treatment (e.g., antihypertensives).Non-Medical Uses:Placebos in clinical trials.Some tablets used in agriculture (e.g., pesticide tablets).Why Popular? Easy to store, transport, and consume.
4/24/25, 5:13 PM - Sarvesh: Slide 4: Advantages of TabletsConvenience: Small, portable, no need for measuring doses.Stability: Longer shelf life compared to liquids or injections.Cost-Effective: Cheaper to produce and package.Variety: Immediate release, sustained release, chewable, etc.Patient-Friendly: Coated tablets for easy swallowing, flavored for kids.

Slide 5: Disadvantages of TabletsBioavailability: Some drugs don’t absorb well in tablet form.Swallowing Issues: Problem for kids, elderly, or patients with dysphagia.Delayed Action: Slower compared to injections or liquids.Side Effects: Some coatings or fillers may cause allergies.Manufacturing Risks: Contamination or improper mixing can affect quality.

Slide 6: Ingredients of TabletsActive Pharmaceutical Ingredient (API): The main drug (e.g., ibuprofen, amoxicillin).Excipients:Binders: Hold tablet together (e.g., starch, cellulose).Fillers/Diluents: Add bulk (e.g., lactose, calcium carbonate).Disintegrants: Help tablet break down in the stomach (e.g., croscarmellose sodium).Lubricants: Prevent sticking during manufacturing (e.g., magnesium stearate).Coatings: For taste, protection, or controlled release (e.g., sugar, polymers).Colorants/Flavoring: For aesthetics or taste (e.g., in chewable tablets).
4/24/25, 5:13 PM - Sarvesh: Slide 2: Introduction to TabletsWhat are Tablets?Oral solid dosage form of medicines, compressed into small, easy-to-swallow shapes.Most common drug delivery method due to convenience and stability.Brief History:Originated in the 19th century; mass production started with modern pharma in the 20th century.Fun Fact: Over 70% of medicines are sold as tablets globally!
